			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2015 Baltimore protests</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_riots&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 Baltimore riots">2015 Baltimore riots</a>)</span></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">This article is about the protests that followed Freddie Gray's hospitalization and subsequent death in police custody. For information about the death itself, see <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Freddie_Gray" title="Death of Freddie Gray">Death of Freddie Gray</a>.</div>

<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #CEE0F2; vertical-align: middle">Injuries and arrests</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Injuries</th>
<td>113 police officers injured,<sup id="cite_ref-WP_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-7">[7]</a></sup> 2 people shot. One fire victim in <a href="/wiki/Critical_condition#Critical" class="mw-redirect" title="Critical condition">critical condition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Arrest" title="Arrest">Arrested</a></th>
<td>486<sup id="cite_ref-WP_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-7">[7]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Criminal_charge" title="Criminal charge">Charged</a></th>
<td>Greg Bailey: charged with obstructing firefighting operations, malicious <a href="/wiki/Property_damage" title="Property damage">destruction of property</a> and reckless <a href="/wiki/Endangerment" title="Endangerment">endangerment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top:1px solid #aaa"><a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">State of emergency</a> declared effective on April 27; rescinded May 6.<sup id="cite_ref-emergencystate_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emergencystate-10">[10]</a></sup><br />
A mandatory curfew was ordered beginning April 28 and ended May 3.<sup id="cite_ref-lati_Balt_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lati_Balt-11">[11]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On April 12, 2015, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore Police Department</a> officers arrested Freddie Gray, a 25-year-old <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> resident of <a href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltimore, Maryland">Baltimore, Maryland</a>. Gray sustained injuries to his neck and spine while in transport in a police vehicle. On April 18, 2015, after Gray's subsequent coma, the residents of Baltimore protested in front of the Western district police station.<sup id="cite_ref-Fenton_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fenton-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Valcourt_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valcourt-2">[2]</a></sup> Gray <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Freddie_Gray" title="Death of Freddie Gray">died the following day</a>, April 19, 2015, a week after the arrest.</p>
<p>Further protests were organized after Gray's death became public knowledge, amid the police department's continuing inability to adequately or consistently explain the events following the arrest and the injuries. Spontaneous protests started after the funeral service, although several included violent elements. Civil unrest continued with at least twenty police officers injured, at least 250 people arrested, 285 to 350 businesses damaged, 150 vehicle fires, 60 structure fires,<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo_damages_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo_damages-12">[12]</a></sup> 27 drugstores looted,<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_June12_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_June12-13">[13]</a></sup> thousands of police and <a href="/wiki/Maryland_National_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Maryland National Guard">Maryland National Guard</a> troops deployed, and with a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency#United_States" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> declared in the city limits of Baltimore.<sup id="cite_ref-LAapril28_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAapril28-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReutersThousands_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersThousands-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 1, 2015, Gray's death was ruled to be a <a href="/wiki/Homicide" title="Homicide">homicide</a> and legal charges were issued against the six officers involved in the incident, including that of second-degree murder.<sup id="cite_ref-Blinder.NYT_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blinder.NYT-16">[16]</a></sup> The state of emergency was lifted on May 6.<sup id="cite_ref-NPR_emergency_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_emergency-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Critical_opinions"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Critical opinions</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Online_reaction"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Online reaction</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Increase_in_violence_and_decrease_in_policing"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Increase in violence and decrease in policing</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_12:_Gray.27s_arrest">April 12: Gray's arrest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: April 12: Gray's arrest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 12, 2015, Freddie Carlos Gray, Jr., a 25-year-old African-American man, was arrested by the Baltimore Police Department in the 1700 block of Presbury Street in the <a href="/wiki/Sandtown-Winchester,_Baltimore" title="Sandtown-Winchester, Baltimore">Sandtown-Winchester neighborhood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup> Gray was seen to be in good health at the time of the arrest. While being transported in a police van, Gray sustained injuries to his neck, including his vocal box, and spinal cord and fell into a coma and was taken to a trauma center. The BPD could not immediately account for the injuries and released contradictory and inconsistent information regarding the timeline of the arrest and transportation and whether Gray had been given appropriately prompt medical treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-Fenton_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fenton-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Valcourt_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valcourt-2">[2]</a></sup> On May 23, 2016, officer Edward Nero was found not guilty on all charges against him in connection with the death of Freddie Gray.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Shortly after that, the remaining officers who had not yet stood trial had all charges dropped against them.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_18_.E2.80.93_24:_Protests_begin">April 18 – 24: Protests begin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: April 18 – 24: Protests begin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 18, 2015, immediately outside the Western District police station, hundreds of Baltimore citizens protested against the apparent mistreatment of Freddie Gray as well against inadequate and inconsistent information on police actions during the arrest and transport. Gray died at approximately 7am on April 19, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup> Later that day, in response to Gray's death, Baltimore Police Commissioner Anthony Batts said "I extend my deepest sympathies to his family" while also saying that "All Lives Matter" in a nod to the "Black Lives Matter" mantra shouted at protests.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Protests continued during six nights in Baltimore's streets. On April 21, 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore Police Department</a> released the identities of the six officers involved in Gray's arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup> That evening, protesters marched from the site of Gray's arrest to the Western District police station. On April 23, Two people were arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Tensions flared, but according to the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore Police Department</a>, the remaining protesters that day were peaceful.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> On April 24, a coalition of organizations including the ACLU, the NAACP, CASA de Maryland, and Leaders of a Beautiful Struggle requested that Governor Larry Hogan act to address issues of police brutality.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_25:_Violence_escalates">April 25: Violence escalates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: April 25: Violence escalates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:854px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Baltimore_Riots_Smash_McDonalds.webm/854px--Baltimore_Riots_Smash_McDonalds.webm.jpg&quot; data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;569656&quot; data-framerate=&quot;30&quot;/&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2b/Baltimore_Riots_Smash_McDonalds.webm/Baltimore_Riots_Smash_McDonalds.webm.360p.webm&quot; <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_Riots_Smash_McDonalds.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rioters breaking the windows of a <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> restaurant on the evening of April 25, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On April 25, 2015, protests were organized in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Baltimore" title="Downtown Baltimore">downtown Baltimore</a>. Protesters marched from the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Hall" title="Baltimore City Hall">Baltimore City Hall</a> to <a href="/wiki/Inner_Harbor" title="Inner Harbor">Inner Harbor</a>. After the final stage of the official protest event, some people became violent, damaging at least five police vehicles and <a href="/wiki/Criminal_rock_throwing" title="Criminal rock throwing">pelting police with rocks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stolberg_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stolberg-24">[24]</a></sup> Near <a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">Oriole Park at Camden Yards</a>, some groups of violent protesters also smashed storefronts and fought with baseball fans arriving at the stadium for a scheduled game between the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>. As a result of the violence, those attending the baseball game were forced<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> to remain inside the stadium for their safety.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> At least 34 people were arrested during the riots, and six police officers were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>J.M. Giordano, a photographer for <i><a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Paper" title="Baltimore City Paper">Baltimore City Paper</a></i>, was taking pictures of the protest when he was "swarmed" and beaten by two police officers in <a href="/wiki/Riot_gear" class="mw-redirect" title="Riot gear">riot gear</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Serpick_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Serpick-29">[29]</a></sup> Sait Serkan Gurbuz, a <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> photographer with visible press credentials, who photographed the scuffle from a public sidewalk, was tackled, handcuffed and walked to the Western District station. He was cited for failure to obey and later released. Subsequently, <i>City Paper</i> published a video on its website documenting the violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Serpick_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Serpick-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a press conference, Baltimore mayor <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Rawlings-Blake" title="Stephanie Rawlings-Blake">Stephanie Rawlings-Blake</a> said most protesters were respectful but a "small group of agitators intervened".<sup id="cite_ref-:6_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-27">[27]</a></sup> She also stated that "It’s a very delicate balancing act. Because while we try to make sure that they were protected from the cars and other things that were going on, we also gave those who wished to destroy space to do that as well. And we worked very hard to keep that balance and to put ourselves in the best position to de-escalate.”<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The phrase "we also gave those who wished to destroy space to do that as well" was interpreted by some conservative-leaning news sources<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> as an indication that the mayor was giving permission to protesters to destroy property, while some others, including <a href="/wiki/Breitbart_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="Breitbart (website)">Breitbart News Network</a>, pointed out that "when you look at the full context, it’s clear the Mayor meant something different (though it’s also true she didn’t say it very clearly)."<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two days later, the mayor's Director of Strategic Planning and Policy, Howard Libit, released a statement clarifying the mayor's remarks:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>What she is saying within this statement was that there was an effort to give the peaceful demonstrators room to conduct their peaceful protests on Saturday. Unfortunately, as a result of providing the peaceful demonstrators with the space to share their message, that also meant that those seeking to incite violence also had the space to operate. The police sought to balance the rights of the peaceful demonstrators against the need to step in against those who were seeking to create violence.</p>
<p>The mayor is not saying that she asked police to give space to people who sought to create violence. Any suggestion otherwise would be a misinterpretation of her statement.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><br /></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_27">April 27</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: April 27">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Funeral">Funeral</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Funeral">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A funeral service was held for Freddie Gray at the New Shiloh Baptist Church on April 27 at <time datetime="2015-04-27 11:00">11&#160;a.m.</time>, after a one-hour public viewing.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> A large attendance included civil rights leaders, families of other people killed by police, and politicians including Congressman <a href="/wiki/Elijah_Cummings" title="Elijah Cummings">Elijah Cummings</a>, Cabinet Secretary Broderick Johnson, White House adviser Heather Foster, and Elias Alcantara of the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Intergovernmental_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of Intergovernmental Affairs">Office of Intergovernmental Affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gray is buried at Woodlawn Cemetery in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_County,_Maryland" title="Baltimore County, Maryland">Baltimore County, Maryland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Preemptive_actions">Preemptive actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Preemptive actions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A photograph of the April 25 rioters standing on a Baltimore police car was superimposed with the text "All HighSchools Monday @3 We Are Going To Purge From <a href="/wiki/Mondawmin_Mall" title="Mondawmin Mall">Mondawmin</a> To The Ave, Back To Downtown #Fdl" ("Purge" being a reference to <a href="/wiki/The_Purge_(film_series)" title="The Purge (film series)">the film series</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and distributed on social media<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and as flyers.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In response, Mondawmin Mall was closed at 2:15&#160;p.m.<sup id="cite_ref-abc2_Conc_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc2_Conc-44">[44]</a></sup> and police in riot gear were deployed to the area. In preparation for the 'purge' police shut down the Mondawmin metro stop and also blockaded many of the nearby streets.<sup id="cite_ref-Brodey_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brodey-45">[45]</a></sup> As a result, students from <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass_High_School_(Baltimore,_Maryland)" title="Frederick Douglass High School (Baltimore, Maryland)">Frederick Douglass High School</a>, which is across the street from Mondawmin Mall, had considerable difficulty leaving the area via public transportation when their classes ended an hour after the "purge" began, and contributed to the swelling crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-Brodey_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brodey-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to eyewitness reports,<sup id="cite_ref-Brodey_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brodey-45">[45]</a></sup> expecting the "purge" to start at 3 p.m., Baltimore police pre-emptively de-boarded all buses going through the area, shut down the nearby <a href="/wiki/Mondawmin_(Baltimore_Metro_Subway_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mondawmin (Baltimore Metro Subway station)">Mondawmin Metro station</a> and cordoned off the area around the mall. Eyewitnesses saw police detain students in that general area. The police, in full riot gear, detained the students for a full half-hour before the first brick was thrown. Meghann Harris, a teacher at nearby <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass_High_School_(Baltimore,_Maryland)" title="Frederick Douglass High School (Baltimore, Maryland)">Frederick Douglass High School</a>, said on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, "If I were a Douglass student that just got trapped in the middle of a minefield BY cops without any way to get home and completely in harm's way, I'd be ready to pop off, too."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other closings in preparation or response to the riot included the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_Baltimore" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Maryland Baltimore">University of Maryland Baltimore</a>, which closed its campus in downtown Baltimore at <time datetime="2015-04-27 14:00">2:00&#160;p.m.</time> citing a police warning regarding "activities (that) may be potentially violent and UMB could be in the path of any violence",<sup id="cite_ref-:8_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Community_College" title="Baltimore City Community College">Baltimore City Community College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coppin_State_University" title="Coppin State University">Coppin State University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lexington_Market" title="Lexington Market">Lexington Market</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Aquarium_in_Baltimore" class="mw-redirect" title="National Aquarium in Baltimore">National Aquarium</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Enoch_Pratt_Free_Library" title="Enoch Pratt Free Library">Enoch Pratt Free Library</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-abc2_Conc_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc2_Conc-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyti_Nati_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyti_Nati-49">[49]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_sculpture_race#East_Coast_Championship_in_Baltimore" title="Kinetic sculpture race">Baltimore Kinetic Sculpture Race</a> was rescheduled from May 2 to June 14.<sup id="cite_ref-bsun-ksrpostponed_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bsun-ksrpostponed-50">[50]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> baseball game against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> scheduled for the evening at <a href="/wiki/Oriole_Park_at_Camden_Yards" title="Oriole Park at Camden Yards">Oriole Park at Camden Yards</a>, and the first of a three-game series,<sup id="cite_ref-espn-oriolespostponedwed_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espn-oriolespostponedwed-51">[51]</a></sup> was also postponed due to the unrest.<sup id="cite_ref-bsun-postponed_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bsun-postponed-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spread_of_violence">Spread of violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Spread of violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Initially 75–100 people who appeared to be high school students began throwing bricks and bottles at police near Mondawmin Mall<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> after police refused high school students access to their primary means of getting home (the transportation hub at Mondawmin Mall),<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> while ordering them to disperse and go home. The violence rapidly spread,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and by later that day two patrol cars were destroyed and fifteen officers were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-48">[48]</a></sup> A police cruiser was destroyed, and some officers suffered broken bones.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BaconJ_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaconJ-57">[57]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/CVS_Pharmacy" title="CVS Pharmacy">CVS Pharmacy</a> location in West Baltimore was looted and burned by rioters;<sup id="cite_ref-cnn._Balt_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn._Balt-58">[58]</a></sup> no one in the CVS was hurt because employees had been evacuated before the CVS was looted and burned,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> but a fire hose used later to put out the CVS fire was punctured by a rioter.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In East Baltimore, the Mary Harvin Senior Center, an under-construction senior housing and services project, burned to the ground; it was rebuilt and opened in April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_28">April 28</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: April 28">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Morning">Morning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Morning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maryland_National_Guard_(17285160576).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Maryland_National_Guard_%2817285160576%29.jpg/220px-Maryland_National_Guard_%2817285160576%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Maryland_National_Guard_%2817285160576%29.jpg/330px-Maryland_National_Guard_%2817285160576%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Maryland_National_Guard_%2817285160576%29.jpg/440px-Maryland_National_Guard_%2817285160576%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1807" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maryland_National_Guard_(17285160576).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A soldier from 1st Battalion, <a href="/wiki/175th_Infantry_Regiment_(United_States)" title="175th Infantry Regiment (United States)">175th Infantry Regiment</a> keeps watch in front of <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Hall" title="Baltimore City Hall">Baltimore City Hall</a> on April&#160;28</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At about <time datetime="2015-04-28 06:00">6:00&#160;a.m.</time>, Baltimore television showed firefighters putting out fires and residents, mostly minority citizens, cleaning up after the overnight rioting.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28-62">[62]</a></sup> Soldiers from the 1st Battalion, 175th Infantry Regiment, Maryland Army National Guard arrived in Baltimore to provide security to vital infrastructure and to give additional support to police.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28-62">[62]</a></sup> At about <time datetime="2015-04-28 07:35">7:35&#160;a.m.</time>, the Baltimore mayor's office reported that there were 144 vehicle fires, 15 structural fires, and nearly 200 arrests.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn_20150428_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_20150428-63">[63]</a></sup> One person had been badly hurt due to an arson.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_20150428_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_20150428-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>At <time datetime="2015-04-28 08:25">8:25&#160;a.m.</time>, it was announced that Maryland Gov. Larry Hogan was temporarily moving his office from Annapolis to Baltimore and that Hogan would visit scenes around Baltimore.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28-62">[62]</a></sup> At approximately 9:00&#160;a.m., Hogan visited an intersection on West Baltimore that was heavily affected by the rioting with damaged vehicles and a looted convenience store, thanking those in the area for help cleaning up the streets.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28_62-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>In one incident that went viral during the previous night, Baltimore mother, Toya Graham, repeatedly struck and berated her son on TV for throwing rocks at police. Graham stated that she didn't want her son to end up like Freddie Gray, but also that he shouldn't seek justice by rioting.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> At <time datetime="2015-04-28 11:15">11:15&#160;a.m.</time> on April 28, Baltimore Police Commissioner Anthony Batts praised Graham, stating, "I wish I had more parents that took charge of their kids out there."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Baltimore County police spokesman Cpl. John Wachter also announced that <a href="/wiki/Security_Square_Mall" title="Security Square Mall">Security Square Mall</a> was going to be closed for the rest of the day following the spreading of rumors that planned actions were going to occur there. The Social Security Administration and the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services also closed.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Afternoon_and_evening">Afternoon and evening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Afternoon and evening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>At <time datetime="2015-04-28 12:00">12:00&#160;p.m.</time> in the area where Freddie Gray was arrested, volunteers numbering in the hundreds were seen cleaning up debris left from the rioting.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28_62-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28-62">[62]</a></sup> Police blocked off some of the area to assist with the cleanup while hardware stores in the neighborhood donated trash bags and brooms and city workers drove in trucks to carry away piles of trash and shattered glass.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28_62-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>At <time datetime="2015-04-28 12:55">12:55&#160;p.m.</time>, President Obama stated that there have been too many worrying interactions between police and black citizens, but said there was "no excuse" for the violence of rioters in Baltimore. At about 1:30&#160;p.m., crowds gathered at a damaged drug store where Rev. <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Jackson" title="Jesse Jackson">Jesse Jackson</a> was visiting, with Jackson stating, "It was painful because it destroyed a lot of neighborhood businesses and hurt a lot of people, but the violence is driven by that alienation." At a <time datetime="2015-04-28 14:30">2:30&#160;p.m.</time> speaking event by Capt. Eric Kowalczyk discussing incidents that occurred on April 27, demonstrators gathered peacefully, though one individual was arrested and pepper spray was used when some protesters became disorderly. At <time datetime="2015-04-28 15:00">3:00&#160;p.m.</time>, Mayor Stephanie Rawlings-Blake took back comments calling rioters "thugs", saying that occasionally, "my little anger interpreter gets the best of me." Baltimore religious leaders announced that 14 churches throughout the city were open to give food to children that relied on schools to provide daily meals.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28point5_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28point5-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>At <time datetime="2015-04-28 20:30">8:30&#160;p.m.</time>, the CEO of Baltimore City Public Schools, Gregory Thornton, announced that Baltimore City Public School classes and after-school events would occur on April 29. Just before <time datetime="2015-04-28 21:00">9:00&#160;p.m.</time>, several hundred protesters gathered around the CVS store that was looted, with some individuals separating the protesters and police, while a local pastor told demonstrators over a loud speaker to respect the curfew, saying, "Let's show the world, because the eyes of the world are on Baltimore right now." A police spokesman, Captain Eric Kowalczyk, stated that authorities were attempting to inform Baltimore residents of the <time datetime="2015-04-28 22:00">10:00&#160;p.m.</time> curfew in multiple ways, through police in patrol cars, sending messages through a police helicopter over the city and by calling residents through a <a href="/wiki/Reverse_911" title="Reverse 911">Reverse 911</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28point5_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28point5-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg/220px-Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg/330px-Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg/440px-Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="756" data-file-height="504" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_riot_police_VOA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Baltimore riot policemen form a line to push back protesters and media members on April&#160;28</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At <time datetime="2015-04-28 22:15">10:15&#160;p.m.</time>, hundreds of demonstrators, some throwing bottles at police, remained in the streets while police in riot gear began to move the crowds with speakers from helicopters overhead broadcasting, "You must go home. You cannot remain here. You will be subject to arrest." Tensions began to grow after individuals began to throw objects at police. Shortly after <time datetime="2015-04-28 22:30">10:30&#160;p.m.</time>, smoke bombs or fireworks were thrown from the crowd and police equipped with riot shields began to slowly advance on the gathering with some people beginning to disperse. At <time datetime="2015-04-28 22:32">10:32&#160;p.m.</time>, Baltimore Police tweeted that "Officers are now deploying pepper balls at the aggressive crowd". They then tweeted at <time datetime="2015-04-28 22:34">10:34&#160;p.m.</time> "People who remain on the street – who do not meet the exceptions – are now in violation of the emergency curfew" with police moving across the intersection and the crowd dispersing down side streets away from the area. At <time datetime="2015-04-28 22:50">10:50&#160;p.m.</time>, military vehicles were seen driving through the streets to disperse the remaining crowd numbered with dozens of people. At <time datetime="2015-04-28 23:00">11:00&#160;p.m.</time>, the CVS intersection was clear except for police and media workers who were exempt from the curfew. At <time datetime="2015-04-28 23:40">11:40&#160;p.m.</time>, Baltimore Police Commissioner Anthony Batts stated that the curfew seemed to work and that ten people were arrested; seven for violating the curfew, two people for looting and one for disorderly conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-APapril28point5_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APapril28point5-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between start of curfew and late night, thirty-five people, including one juvenile, had been arrested for violating the curfew.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_29_.E2.80.93_May_3">April 29 – May 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: April 29 – May 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the riots, many small business owners struggled to clean up.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Over 200 small businesses were unable to reopen by April 29.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Residents of all ages, genders, and races came together to help clean Baltimore's streets.<sup id="cite_ref-Cleanup_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cleanup-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Eighteen were arrested for curfew violations on April 29.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maryland_National_Guard_(17145635149).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Maryland_National_Guard_%2817145635149%29.jpg/220px-Maryland_National_Guard_%2817145635149%29.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Maryland_National_Guard_%2817145635149%29.jpg/330px-Maryland_National_Guard_%2817145635149%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Maryland_National_Guard_%2817145635149%29.jpg/440px-Maryland_National_Guard_%2817145635149%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1670" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maryland_National_Guard_(17145635149).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Protesters gathered in front of <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_City_Hall" title="Baltimore City Hall">Baltimore City Hall</a> on April&#160;30</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From April 29-May 3, 2015 FBI surveillance aircraft used <a href="/wiki/Forward_looking_infrared" title="Forward looking infrared">FLIR</a> cameras to record video of civil unrest. In August 2016, 18 hours of footage was released following a FOIA request from the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>By April 30, over forty <a href="/wiki/Korean_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean American">South Korean</a>-<a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Koreans_in_Baltimore" title="History of the Koreans in Baltimore">owned businesses</a> had been damaged by the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese American">Chinese American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab American">Arab American</a> owned stores were also targeted, with looters directed by African American gangs towards those businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> That night, four were arrested for curfew violations.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Forty people were arrested for such night violations on May 1.<sup id="cite_ref-go_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-go-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the largest peaceful rally on Saturday, May 2, 2015, 46 people were arrested during the night time curfew.<sup id="cite_ref-Curfew_May2_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curfew_May2-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>One person arrested on May 2 was News2Share journalist Ford Fischer. He was handcuffed and initially charged with violating curfew, despite the police confirming that "he's credentialed media."<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> After confirming the charge as "curfew violation" to another journalist, they changed it to a civil citation for "Disorderly Conduct." As of May 21, he still faces that citation.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> This all came after the police department had confirmed that media are exempt from the curfew via Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>The night curfew on the city was lifted on May 3.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Meanwhile, all charges against violators were dropped. It was found that in section 14-107 of the state's public safety code, only the governor and not the mayor has the authority to issue a curfew. It was decided that the arrests of violators were punishment enough.<sup id="cite_ref-Curfew_Mayor_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curfew_Mayor-89">[89]</a></sup> Those who committed violations of the law other than curfew violations have still been prosecuted.<sup id="cite_ref-CBSauth_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSauth-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Maryland National Guard withdrew completely from Baltimore on May 4.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Result_of_investigation_and_charges_filed">Result of investigation and charges filed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Result of investigation and charges filed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Initially, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Police_Department" title="Baltimore Police Department">Baltimore Police Department</a> suspended six officers with pay pending an investigation of Gray's death.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The six officers involved in the arrest were identified as Lieutenant Brian Rice, Sergeant Alicia White, Officer William Porter, Officer Garrett Miller, Officer Edward Nero, and Officer Caesar Goodson.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> On April 24, 2015, Police Commissioner Anthony Batts said, "We know our police employees failed to get him medical attention in a timely manner multiple times."<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Batts also acknowledged police did not follow procedure when they failed to buckle Gray in the van while he was being transported to the police station. The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Justice">U.S. Department of Justice</a> also opened an investigation into the case.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 1, 2015, after receiving a medical examiner's report ruling Gray's death a <a href="/wiki/Homicide" title="Homicide">homicide</a>, state prosecutors said that they had probable cause to file criminal charges against the six officers involved. Mosby said that the Baltimore police had acted illegally and that "No crime had been committed [by Freddie Gray]".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Mosby said that Gray "suffered a critical neck injury as a result of being handcuffed, shackled by his feet and unrestrained inside the BPD wagon."<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Mosby said officers had "failed to establish probable cause for Mr. Gray's arrest, as no crime had been committed",<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and charged officers with <a href="/wiki/False_imprisonment" title="False imprisonment">false imprisonment</a>, because Gray was carrying a <a href="/wiki/Pocket_knife" class="mw-redirect" title="Pocket knife">pocket knife</a> of legal size, and not the switchblade police claimed he had possessed at the time of his arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> All six officers were taken into custody and processed at Baltimore Central Booking and Intake Center.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>The trial of Officer William G. Porter, a black officer and the first of the 6 charged officers to go to trial, ended in a mistrial.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The Prosecution had intended to have Porter testify against both his supervisor on the day, Sgt. Alicia White, and the driver of the van, Officer Caesar Goodson Jr. Both are fellow black officers.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The trials have run into significant delays due to multiple motions being filed by both sides in the cases. Prosecutors intend to retry Porter when they are able to do so. On May 23, 2016, Officer Edward Nero was found not guilty on all four counts he was charged with, including two counts of misconduct in office, misdemeanor reckless endangerment, and misdemeanor assault in the second degree.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_protests">Related protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Related protests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png/220px-NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png/330px-NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png/440px-NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NYC_Police_surrounding_protesters_at_2015_Flatiron_District_protests.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Policemen surround protesters at East 19th Street in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On April 29, 2015, protesters marched through <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, blocking off traffic in key areas, including the <a href="/wiki/Holland_Tunnel" title="Holland Tunnel">Holland Tunnel</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Side_Highway" title="West Side Highway">West Side Highway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Carmen Perez, director of the criminal justice reform group Justice League, said, "It's all about solidarity, We're here to spread the message of peace from Baltimore's initial protests."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> More than 100 people were arrested,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> and the police did not allow the protest to take form before making arrests.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anti-police brutality protests were also held in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> in solidarity with the Baltimore protests. Eleven people were arrested on April 29, 2015 following physical altercations in which police used pepper spray on protesters who rallied around <a href="/wiki/Colfax_Avenue" title="Colfax Avenue">Colfax Avenue</a> and Broadway street. The confrontation occurred shortly after 7&#160;p.m. when an officer was knocked off his motorcycle by a protester and assaulted by five others. Police reported force was used in response to the incident. By 7:40&#160;p.m., Broadway street was cleared for traffic as protesters relocated to the 16th Street Mall.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were also solidarity protests in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Ann_Arbor" class="mw-redirect" title="Ann Arbor">Ann Arbor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque" class="mw-redirect" title="Albuquerque">Albuquerque</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ABQ_protest_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABQ_protest-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oakland" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland">Oakland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preventive_actions">Preventive actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Preventive actions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_actions">Government actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Government actions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>At a press conference in the evening, the mayor announced there would be a citywide curfew of 10:00&#160;p.m. to 5:00&#160;a.m. starting April 28.<sup id="cite_ref-lati_Balt_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lati_Balt-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amer_Viol_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amer_Viol-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-balt_Balt_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balt_Balt-121">[121]</a></sup> The Baltimore solicitor's office stated that a limitation of the curfew to only certain neighborhoods could potentially be viewed as racial discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-Curfew_Mayor_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curfew_Mayor-89">[89]</a></sup> Neighboring Anne Arundel and Baltimore Counties cancelled school field trips and activities scheduled in Baltimore City until May 3.<sup id="cite_ref-abc2_Conc_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc2_Conc-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wbal_Gov._122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wbal_Gov.-122">[122]</a></sup> Officials also announced that Baltimore's city schools would be closed on Tuesday.<sup id="cite_ref-usat_Balt_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usat_Balt-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maryland Governor <a href="/wiki/Larry_Hogan" title="Larry Hogan">Larry Hogan</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> and activated the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_National_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Maryland National Guard">Maryland National Guard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-emergencystate_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emergencystate-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-maryland-emergencystate_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maryland-emergencystate-124">[124]</a></sup> Major General <a href="/wiki/Linda_L._Singh" title="Linda L. Singh">Linda Singh</a> of the Maryland National Guard commented that there would be a "massive number" of soldiers in Maryland on the night of April 27, and that up to 5,000 soldiers could be deployed.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maryland_State_Police" title="Maryland State Police">Maryland State Police</a> activated 500 officers for duty in Baltimore, and requested an additional 5,000 state police officers from other states.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Business owners in the city complained that the curfew required establishments with later hours to close their doors early, thereby costing them revenue from later hours customers and hurting their employees by forcing them to work fewer hours.<sup id="cite_ref-eater_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rawstory_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rawstory-128">[128]</a></sup> Some businesses complained that the curfew cost them as much as $50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> While those with night jobs were given an exemption to be allowed to travel to work, early closing hours continued to cost employees work hours.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera-71">[71]</a></sup> Despite criticism of curfew enforcement, Mayor Rawlings-Blake stood by the curfew, saying it was necessary to maintain control.<sup id="cite_ref-CBSauth_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSauth-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_actions">Sports actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sports actions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Baltimore Ravens</a> had canceled their <a href="/wiki/2015_NFL_draft" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 NFL draft">NFL Draft</a> party in response to the riots.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>After consulting with <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, the Baltimore Orioles announced that their second game against the Chicago White Sox would also be postponed, and that their game on April 29 would be played in the afternoon <a href="/wiki/Behind_closed_doors_(sport)" title="Behind closed doors (sport)">behind closed doors</a>. This was believed to be the first behind closed doors game in Major League Baseball history (it is occasionally seen in soccer as punishment for spectator behaviour).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The attendance for the game was officially recorded as zero, thus breaking the previous record (of six, set in 1882) for the lowest attendance at a Major League Baseball game.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The two cancelled games were made up as a <a href="/wiki/Doubleheader_(baseball)" title="Doubleheader (baseball)">doubleheader</a> on May 28. The team also moved its May 1–3 series against the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> from Camden Yards to <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Field" title="Tropicana Field">Tropicana Field</a>, but still played as the home team (despite the Rays hosting it).<sup id="cite_ref-espn-oriolespostponedwed_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espn-oriolespostponedwed-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gang_involvement">Gang involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Gang involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After Baltimore police determined there was a "credible threat" of <a href="/wiki/Gang_violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Gang violence">gang violence</a> against police officers across the country, many departments across the US heightened their security in response: for example the Los Angeles Police Department ordered their officers to ride in pairs.<sup id="cite_ref-lati_LAPD_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lati_LAPD-135">[135]</a></sup> Baltimore police claimed evidence to support the idea that the <a href="/wiki/Black_Guerrilla_Family" title="Black Guerrilla Family">Black Guerrilla Family</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bloods" title="Bloods">Bloods</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Crips" title="Crips">Crips</a> were "teaming up" to target police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Later, however, leaders of both the Bloods and the Crips denied the allegations,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> released a video statement asking for calm and peaceful protest in the area,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> and joined with police and clergy to enforce the curfew.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> At one occasion, gang members helped to prevent a riot at the <a href="/wiki/Security_Square_Mall" title="Security Square Mall">Security Square Mall</a> by dispersing would-be rioters.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> On other occasions, rival gang members helped each other to protect black-owned businesses, black children, and reporters, diverting rioters to Korean-, Chinese-, and Arab-owned businesses instead.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> On yet another occasion, the Bloods, the Crips, and the <a href="/wiki/Nation_of_Islam" title="Nation of Islam">Nation of Islam</a> were seen taking a picture together and working together to dispel violence while peacefully demonstrating.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The racial prejudice shown in the protection of persons and businesses highlights the deep racial tensions between not only the black and white populations in general but between numerous ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_opinions">Critical opinions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Critical opinions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 28, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> strongly condemned the violence during a White House press conference, saying, "There's no excuse for the kind of violence that we saw yesterday. It is counterproductive. ... When individuals get crowbars and start prying open doors to loot, they're not protesting. They're not making a statement. They're stealing. When they burn down a building, they're committing arson. And they're destroying and undermining businesses and opportunities in their own communities. That robs jobs and opportunity from people in that area." Obama went on to applaud the actions of peaceful protesters whom he felt were being undermined by the violence, and called upon the nation to take meaningful action to collectively solve poverty and law enforcement issues fueling what he described as "a crisis".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>On social media and elsewhere, Mayor Rawlings-Blake and President Obama were criticized for calling the rioters "thugs" on April 28.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>When asked about the postponement of the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> game, the Orioles' chief operating officer, <a href="/wiki/John_P._Angelos" title="John P. Angelos">John P. Angelos</a>, said:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>My greater source of personal concern, outrage and sympathy ... is focused neither upon one night's property damage nor upon the acts, but is focused rather upon the past four-decade period during which an American political elite have shipped middle class and working class jobs away from Baltimore and cities and towns around the U.S. to third-world dictatorships ... plunged tens of millions of good hard working Americans into economic devastation and then followed that action around the nation by diminishing every American’s civil rights protections in order to control an unfairly impoverished population living under an ever-declining standard of living and suffering at the butt end of an ever-more militarized and aggressive surveillance state. The innocent working families of all backgrounds whose lives and dreams have been cut short by excessive violence, surveillance, and other abuses of the Bill of Rights by government pay the true price, an ultimate price, and one that far exceeds the importance of any kids' game played tonight, or ever....<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_reaction">Online reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Online reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The protests were originally covered on social media with the <a href="/wiki/Hashtag" title="Hashtag">hashtag</a> #BaltimoreRiots. However, by April 28, the more popular hashtag to cover the protests became #BaltimoreUprising. The change may have occurred in response to a decline in violent actions, or may have been the promotion of a new political narrative by social media users.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Increase_in_violence_and_decrease_in_policing">Increase in violence and decrease in policing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Baltimore_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Increase in violence and decrease in policing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Baltimore recorded 43 homicides in the month of May, the second deadliest month on record and the worst since December 1971 when 44 homicides were recorded. There have also been more than 100 non-fatal shootings in May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Police commissioner Anthony Batts blames looted drugs, stolen from 27 pharmacies and two methadone clinics, as well as street distribution and turf wars for the spike in crime.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>The increase in shootings has occurred along with a 50% decline in arrests since the charging of six officers in Gray’s death in custody.<sup id="cite_ref-CBSArrestsDrop_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSArrestsDrop-152">[152]</a></sup> The heavy police presence in crime-ridden neighborhoods is no longer apparent with one resident stating, "Before it was over-policing. Now there's no police."<sup id="cite_ref-CBSArrestsDrop_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSArrestsDrop-152">[152]</a></sup> One officer speaking anonymously stated, "After the protests, it seems like the citizens would appreciate a lack of police presence, and that's exactly what they're getting."<sup id="cite_ref-StarAfterRiots_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StarAfterRiots-153">[153]</a></sup> Batts stated that his officers are "not holding back" despite encountering hostility in the Western District whenever they make an arrest with "30 to 50 people surrounding them at any time;"<sup id="cite_ref-CBSArrestsDrop_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSArrestsDrop-152">[152]</a></sup> he also stated that his officers feel "confused and unsupported" in the wake of the charges. The president of the police union said his members are "afraid of going to jail for doing their jobs properly."<sup id="cite_ref-StarAfterRiots_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StarAfterRiots-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <i>The New York Times</i>, looting from 27 drugstores resulted in an increase in black market access to opiates.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-CBSArrestsDrop-152"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CBSArrestsDrop_152-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CBSArrestsDrop_152-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CBSArrestsDrop_152-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://baltimore.cbslocal.com/2015/05/28/baltimore-residents-fearful-amid-rash-of-homicides/">"Baltimore Gets Bloodier As Arrests Drop Post-Freddie Gray"</a>. <i>CBS News</i>. May 28, 2015. <q>What is happening, there is a lot of levels of confusion in the police organization. There are people who have pain, there are people who are hurt, there are people who are frustrated, there are people who are angry," Batts said. "There are people, and they've said this to me, 'If I get out of my car and make a stop for a reasonable suspicion that leads to probable cause but I make a mistake on it, will I be arrested?' They pull up to a scene and another officer has done something that they don’t know, it may be illegal, will they be arrested for it? Those are things they are asking.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3A2015+Baltimore+protests&amp;rft.atitle=Baltimore+Gets+Bloodier+As+Arrests+Drop+Post-Freddie+Gray&amp;rft.date=2015-05-28&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbaltimore.cbslocal.com%2F2015%2F05%2F28%2Fbaltimore-residents-fearful-amid-rash-of-homicides%2F&amp;rft.jtitle=CBS+News&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
